<p><b>Patrick Kluivert</b> (<small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[ˈpɛtrɪk ˈklœy̯vərt]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nl-Patrick_Kluivert.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/81/Nl-Patrick_Kluivert.ogg" class="internal" title="Nl-Patrick Kluivert.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; born 1 July 1976) is a Dutch former <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> player and coach who is the academy director of <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a>.
</p><p>He is the former director of football for <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_F.C." title="Paris Saint-Germain F.C.">Paris Saint-Germain</a> in France. Kluivert was the assistant manager of <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">Cameroon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> He played as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Striker" title="Forward (association football)">striker</a>, most notably for <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">AFC Ajax</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands national team</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Profile_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Profile-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He was already part of Ajax's <a href="/wiki/Golden_generation#AFC_Ajax" title="Golden generation">Golden Generation</a> of the 1990s at the age of 18, scoring the winner in the <a href="/wiki/1995_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="1995 UEFA Champions League Final">1995 UEFA Champions League Final</a>. He spent six years with Spanish club Barcelona where he formed a successful partnership with <a href="/wiki/Rivaldo" title="Rivaldo">Rivaldo</a>, where both won the Spanish <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> <a href="/wiki/1998-99_La_Liga" class="mw-redirect" title="1998-99 La Liga">championship of 1999</a> and Kluivert scored 124 goals from 249 appearances in all.<sup id="cite_ref-Profile_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Profile-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Barca_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barca-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kluivert played for the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Dutch national team</a> from 1994 to 2004. With 40 goals in 79 appearances, he is the third highest top goalscorer for Oranje. He played in three European Championships and the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 FIFA World Cup</a>, and was joint top scorer at <a href="/wiki/Euro_2000" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro 2000">Euro 2000</a> where upon the scoresheet he tallied a total of 5 times. In 2004, he was named in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_100" title="FIFA 100">FIFA 100</a>, a list of the 125 greatest living footballers chosen by <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pelé">Pelé</a> as part of <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>'s centenary observances.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He began his coaching career as an assistant at <a href="/wiki/AZ_(football_club)" class="mw-redirect" title="AZ (football club)">AZ</a> and then <a href="/wiki/N.E.C._(football_club)" title="N.E.C. (football club)">NEC</a>. He had a brief coaching stint in Australia with the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Roar_FC" title="Brisbane Roar FC">Brisbane Roar</a>, before coaching <a href="/wiki/Jong_FC_Twente" title="Jong FC Twente">Jong FC Twente</a> to a national title in the Dutch <a href="/wiki/Beloften_Eredivisie" title="Beloften Eredivisie">reserves league</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> He was assistant manager to <a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands national football team</a> when they finished third at the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a> in Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, he took over as head coach of the <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_national_football_team" title="Curaçao national football team">Curaçao national team</a> for the country's <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification">2018 FIFA World Cup qualifying</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2017_Caribbean_Cup_qualification" title="2017 Caribbean Cup qualification">2017 Caribbean Cup qualifying</a> campaigns. In 2016, it was announced that he would take over the <a href="/wiki/Ajax_Youth_Academy" title="Ajax Youth Academy">Ajax A1</a> (under-19) selection, coaching his son, <a href="/wiki/Justin_Kluivert" title="Justin Kluivert">Justin Kluivert</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Voetbal_International_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Voetbal_International-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> before taking a position as director of football for Paris Saint-Germain.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Kluivert was born on 1 July 1976 in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, Netherlands. His father, a professional football player, was born in <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> and his mother in <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">Curaçao</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Kluivert learned to play football on the street. After a year at football club <a href="/wiki/Schellingwoude" title="Schellingwoude">Schellingwoude</a>, he joined the <a href="/wiki/Ajax_Youth_Academy" title="Ajax Youth Academy">Ajax Youth Academy</a> at the age of seven.
</p><p>He played several different positions as a youth, including <a href="/wiki/Defender_(association_football)" title="Defender (association football)">defender</a>. He was strong in technique, football intelligence, and speed, but was considered too impulsive.<sup id="cite_ref-bio-eng_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio-eng-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Kluivert played for the Dutch national teams under-15, under-16 and under-17.<sup id="cite_ref-bio-eng_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio-eng-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ajax">Ajax</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ajax">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kluivert was part of Ajax's <a href="/wiki/Golden_generation#AFC_Ajax" title="Golden generation">Golden Generation</a> of the 1990s. He made his debut in the senior team of <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a> on 21 August 1994 at the age of 18 in the <a href="/wiki/Johan_Cruijff_Shield" class="mw-redirect" title="Johan Cruijff Shield">Dutch Supercup</a> win against the old arch rival <a href="/wiki/Feyenoord" title="Feyenoord">Feyenoord</a>, in which he scored his first goal. He went on to top score for Ajax in the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Eredivisie" title="1994–95 Eredivisie">1994–95 Eredivisie</a> with 18 goals in 25 appearances,<sup id="cite_ref-thesefootball_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thesefootball-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> as <a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a>'s team won the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dutch_football_champions" title="List of Dutch football champions">Dutch championship</a> without losing a match.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1994–95 season also saw Kluivert make his mark – along with a host of youngsters from the Ajax youth academy, including <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Davids" title="Edgar Davids">Edgar Davids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Seedorf" title="Clarence Seedorf">Clarence Seedorf</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Edwin_van_der_Sar" title="Edwin van der Sar">Edwin van der Sar</a> – on the European stage with a triumph in the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_UEFA_Champions_League" title="1994–95 UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>. Kluivert came off the bench to score an 85th-minute winner in the <a href="/wiki/1995_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="1995 UEFA Champions League Final">1995 Champions League Final</a> against <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">A.C. Milan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, Austria. The youngest player to score in a final of the main event of the European continent, when he was only 18 years, 10 months and 23 days.<sup id="cite_ref-thesefootball_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thesefootball-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He again top-scored for Ajax in <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_AFC_Ajax_season" title="1995–96 AFC Ajax season">1995–96</a> with 15 goals in 28 appearances as the club won five trophies, including the <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_Eredivisie" title="1995–96 Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a> title. He scored the winning goal in extra time of the season opening <a href="/wiki/1995_Dutch_Supercup" title="1995 Dutch Supercup">Dutch Supercup</a> against Feyenoord and also scored the team's away goal in the 5–1 aggregate win over <a href="/wiki/Real_Zaragoza" title="Real Zaragoza">Real Zaragoza</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1995_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="1995 UEFA Super Cup">1995 UEFA Super Cup</a>.
</p><p>On 28 November 1995, Kluivert was the only Ajax player to miss his kick in the 4–3 <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shootout</a> win over <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%AAmio_Foot-Ball_Porto_Alegrense" title="Grêmio Foot-Ball Porto Alegrense">Grêmio</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> that saw <i>de Godenzonen</i> win the <a href="/wiki/1995_Intercontinental_Cup" title="1995 Intercontinental Cup">Intercontinental Cup</a>. Kluivert was also in excellent form during Ajax's defence of their Champions League trophy, scoring in away wins at <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>, but a knee injury prevented him from participating for the full 90 minutes in the team's loss to <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1996_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="1996 UEFA Champions League Final">1996 UEFA Champions League Final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thesefootball_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thesefootball-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the end of an injury hit <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_Eredivisie" title="1996–97 Eredivisie">1996–97 season</a> in which he made only 17 league appearances, Kluivert joined <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">A.C. Milan</a> on a <a href="/wiki/Bosman_ruling" title="Bosman ruling">Bosman transfer</a> after rejecting Ajax's offer of a new contract.<sup id="cite_ref-thesefootball_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thesefootball-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He ended his spell at the Amsterdam club with 39 goals from 70 Eredivisie matches.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Milan">Milan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Milan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kluivert's career at Milan started well, with the striker scoring a sensational goal against <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Trofeo_Luigi_Berlusconi" title="Trofeo Luigi Berlusconi">Trofeo Luigi Berlusconi</a> However, he spent only one season at the <a href="/wiki/San_Siro" title="San Siro">San Siro</a>, scoring six times in 27 <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_Serie_A" title="1997–98 Serie A">Serie A</a> matches,<sup id="cite_ref-thesefootball_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thesefootball-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> as the Rossoneri finished in 10th place.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Barcelona">Barcelona</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Barcelona">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 28 August 1998, an hour before the transfer deadline, Kluivert signed a four-year contract with <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a> for a fee of £8.75 million.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Kluivert was reunited with <a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a>, a mentor from his days at Ajax. Kluivert scored 16 league goals and formed a successful partnership with <a href="/wiki/Rivaldo" title="Rivaldo">Rivaldo</a>, which enabled Barça to defend the Spanish <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> in <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_La_Liga" title="1998–99 La Liga">1998–99</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thesefootball_14-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thesefootball-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The following season was also a successful one for Kluivert. Although Barcelona failed to win a third consecutive league title, Kluivert finished the season as the club's top scorer with 15 league goals.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Kluivert went on to top score twice more in his next four seasons at <a href="/wiki/Camp_Nou" title="Camp Nou">Camp Nou</a> but the team completed a period of five years without a major trophy after their title success in 1999.
</p><p>In the summer of 2004, Kluivert was one of four Dutch players released by Barcelona. He ended his career at <i>Barça</i> with 124 goals from 249 appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-Barca_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barca-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, the Dutchman once again featured for Barca in a legends game against Uganda all stars where he, in lobbing the ball, scored an amazing goal.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newcastle_United">Newcastle United</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Newcastle United">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kluivert joined <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> on a free transfer in July 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-Newcastle_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newcastle-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> He stated that his reasons for joining Newcastle was due to the overwhelming reaction he received whilst playing for Barcelona against Newcastle during a pre season friendly as well as teaming up with Newcastle's star players such as <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Newcastle_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newcastle-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Kluivert scored some classy and crucial goals at and away from <a href="/wiki/St_James%27s_Park" title="St James&#39;s Park">St James's Park</a> namely in winning strikes against both <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a>, with both games ending 1–0 to Newcastle.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He also scored away against <a href="/wiki/Olympiacos_F.C." title="Olympiacos F.C.">Olympiakos</a> in a 3-1 win in the first leg of the round of 16 of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a>. Kluivert eventually scored 5 goals in all in that season's UEFA Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> He altogether scored 13 goals in his debut season, being Newcastle's overall second highest goal scorer for <a href="/wiki/2004-05_UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="2004-05 UEFA Cup">2004/05</a>. Despite these feats, Kluivert was then released by Newcastle in the summer of 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Valencia">Valencia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Valencia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kluivert decided to return to Spain to play at the <a href="/wiki/Mestalla" class="mw-redirect" title="Mestalla">Mestalla</a> for <a href="/wiki/Valencia_CF" title="Valencia CF">Valencia CF</a>. During that <a href="/wiki/2005-06_La_Liga" class="mw-redirect" title="2005-06 La Liga">2005-06 season</a>, Valencia finished third in La Liga thus qualifying for the Champions League after a 1-season absence. Kluivert played for a total of 202 minutes, as he spent most of that season injured.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="PSV">PSV</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: PSV">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Despite widespread rumours that Kluivert was to return home to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Arena">Johan Cruyff Arena</a>, Kluivert's return to the <a href="/wiki/Eredivisie" title="Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a> was to be with <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV</a>, with whom he signed a one-year deal in 2006. Just as with his debut for Ajax, Kluivert made his PSV debut against Feyenoord in a 2–1 win, coming on as a substitute. After that, he had two injuries during the first half of the season, which limited his playing time. In a game against Ajax at the <a href="/wiki/Philips_Stadion" title="Philips Stadion">Philips Stadion</a>, Kluivert <a href="/wiki/Goal_celebration" title="Goal celebration">refused to celebrate after scoring</a> a goal against his former club. He was eventually released in July 2007.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lille">Lille</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Lille">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 25 July 2007, Kluivert joined French side <a href="/wiki/Lille_OSC" title="Lille OSC">Lille</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Kluivert made his full international debut on 16 November 1994 in a European qualifier against the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic_national_football_team" title="Czech Republic national football team">Czech Republic</a>, replacing <a href="/wiki/Youri_Mulder" title="Youri Mulder">Youri Mulder</a> after 13 minutes of a 0&#8211;0 draw in Rotterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In his second match, on 29 March 1995, he replaced <a href="/wiki/Ronald_de_Boer" title="Ronald de Boer">Ronald de Boer</a> after 77 minutes, and seven minutes later scored his first international goal to wrap up a 4&#8211;0 home qualifying win over <a href="/wiki/Malta_national_football_team" title="Malta national football team">Malta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 1995, Kluivert scored both goals in the Netherlands' 2–0 <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996_qualifying_play-off" title="UEFA Euro 1996 qualifying play-off">UEFA Euro 1996 qualifying play-off</a> win over <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Ireland</a> at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a>, to qualify the <i>Oranje</i> for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996" title="UEFA Euro 1996">UEFA Euro 1996</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Kluivert missed most of the tournament with a knee injury but he scored against host nation <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a>, to enable the Netherlands to qualify for the knock-out round over <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a> on goal difference. There, they lost in a penalty shootout to <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a>.
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 FIFA World Cup</a>, Kluivert was <a href="/wiki/Misconduct_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Misconduct (football)">sent off</a> against <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a> by referee <a href="/wiki/Pierluigi_Collina" title="Pierluigi Collina">Pierluigi Collina</a> after elbowing <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Staelens" title="Lorenzo Staelens">Lorenzo Staelens</a>. He made amends when selected to play against <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a> in the quarter-finals of the same tournament where he scored the opening goal. He also impressed in later matches, scoring a late equalising goal from a header to draw his team level with <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a> in the semi-final, although the Netherlands went on to lose the penalty shootout.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2000" title="UEFA Euro 2000">UEFA Euro 2000</a> would represent Kluivert's finest hour as the spearhead of a star-studded <i>Oranje</i> side. Kluivert scored a hat-trick in the 6–1 quarter-final demolition of <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_football_team" title="Yugoslavia national football team">Yugoslavia</a>; he was originally credited with four goals, but the third was later re-attributed as an own goal by Yugoslavia's <a href="/wiki/Dejan_Govedarica" title="Dejan Govedarica">Dejan Govedarica</a> after Kluivert admitted not getting a touch on <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bosvelt" title="Paul Bosvelt">Paul Bosvelt</a>'s cross. Had all four goals stood, Kluivert would have been the first player to score four times in a European Championship finals match.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The semi-final against <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> would provide much heartache for Kluivert, as the Dutch yet again crashed out on penalties. Neither Kluivert nor his Dutch side could find the back of the net, despite twice having a chance from the penalty spot – Kluivert himself would miss one of those penalties during the game, but did score in the penalty shoot-out. Despite the Dutch falling short, Kluivert will be remembered for rising to the occasion in front of partisan home crowds, scoring five goals in as many games, jointly claiming the Golden Boot with <a href="/wiki/Savo_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Savo Milošević">Savo Milošević</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Boot_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boot-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kluivert would once again enter <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">UEFA Euro 2004</a> wearing the famous #9 jersey for his country with the Dutch reaching the semifinals of the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As well as from being left out of the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a> squad by coach <a href="/wiki/Marco_van_Basten" title="Marco van Basten">Marco van Basten</a>, Kluivert was not called up to play in any of the qualifying games leading up to the World Cup either. This was due to the fact that he suffered persistent injuries which prevented him from playing for his club during the 2005-06 season. Kluivert was the all-time leading <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team#Top_goalscorers" title="Netherlands national football team">goalscorer</a> for the Dutch national team with 40 goals, until he was surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Robin_van_Persie" title="Robin van Persie">Robin van Persie</a> in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Although tall in stature, Kluivert possessed a remarkably impressive 'first touch' and quick feet for such a large striker. Similar to Brazilian footballer <a href="/wiki/Ronaldo_(Brazilian_footballer)" title="Ronaldo (Brazilian footballer)">Ronaldo</a>, he often used several <a href="/wiki/Dummy_(football)" title="Dummy (football)">feints</a>, namely the <a href="/wiki/Cruijff_Turn" class="mw-redirect" title="Cruijff Turn">Cruijff Turn</a>, to great effect to <a href="/wiki/Dribbling#Association_football" title="Dribbling">go past defenders</a>, due to his pace, strong technical skills and football intelligence. Kluivert also utilised his height, power, and strong physique to dominate aerial balls and was considered to possess one of the best headers in the then-contemporary game. A versatile player, with an eye for goal, he was capable of playing in several other positions across the pitch. Despite his ability, he drew criticism for his character and attitude throughout his career.<sup id="cite_ref-bio-eng_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio-eng-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coaching_career">Coaching career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Coaching career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Early career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 29 April 2008, Dutch media reported that Kluivert would take part in the coaching course of the Dutch Football Association (KNVB) to become a professional football coach.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Football_Association" title="Royal Dutch Football Association">KNVB</a> requires that all coaching badge candidates complete this sort of apprenticeship.
</p><p>On 18 July 2008, it was reported on the football website <i>Goal.com</i> that Kluivert would be spending the 2008–09 season as a member of the backroom coaching staff of <a href="/wiki/Eredivisie" title="Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a> club <a href="/wiki/AZ_(football_club)" class="mw-redirect" title="AZ (football club)">AZ</a>. Later on, in an interview on <i><a href="/wiki/Soccer_AM" title="Soccer AM">Soccer AM</a></i>, Kluivert revealed his role involved coaching the strikers at AZ.
</p><p>In January 2010, Kluivert took a position as an assistant coach for Australian <a href="/wiki/A-League" title="A-League">A-League</a> side <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Roar_FC" title="Brisbane Roar FC">Brisbane Roar FC</a> under head coach <a href="/wiki/Ange_Postecoglou" title="Ange Postecoglou">Ange Postecoglou</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 19 May 2010, Kluivert told journalists he ruled out a comeback as a football player.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> From August 2010 on, he was an assistant-coach for <a href="/wiki/N.E.C._(football_club)" title="N.E.C. (football club)">N.E.C.</a>, coaching the strikers. In the 2011–12 season, he moved on and took charge of the <a href="/wiki/FC_Twente" title="FC Twente">FC Twente</a> youth and reserve team, coaching <a href="/wiki/Jong_FC_Twente" title="Jong FC Twente">Jong FC Twente</a> to a national title in the <a href="/wiki/Beloften_Eredivisie" title="Beloften Eredivisie">Beloften Eredivisie</a>.
</p><p>In August 2012, Kluivert joined the Netherlands national team coaching staff to work under head coach <a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Kluivert's time with the Netherlands culminated with a third-place finish in the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a> campaign.
</p><p>On 5 March 2015, it was announced that Kluivert would take over as manager of the <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_national_football_team" title="Curaçao national football team">Curaçao national football team</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification">2018 FIFA World Cup qualification</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Metro_Nieuws_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metro_Nieuws-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Curaçao progressed through the first two qualifying rounds, defeating <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_national_football_team" title="Montserrat national football team">Montserrat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuba_national_football_team" title="Cuba national football team">Cuba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On 8 September 2015 Curaçao were eliminated in the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(CONCACAF)#Third_round" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification (CONCACAF)">2018 FIFA World Cup third qualifying round</a> by <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador_national_football_team" title="El Salvador national football team">El Salvador</a>, losing 2–0 on aggregate score.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Having helped the country to their best performance yet in World Cup qualifying, Kluivert announced the end of his tenure as head coach of the team on 10 September 2015. While pursuing other ventures, he remains a close advisor to the <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_Football_Federation" title="Curaçao Football Federation">Curaçao Football Federation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Cura.C3.A7ao"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Curaçao">Curaçao</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Curaçao">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 24 February 2016, Kluivert announced his decision to remain head coach of Curaçao ahead of the teams' <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Cup" title="Caribbean Cup">Caribbean Cup</a> qualifying matches against the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic_national_football_team" title="Dominican Republic national football team">Dominican Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbados_national_football_team" title="Barbados national football team">Barbados</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> On 2 May 2016, it was announced that Kluivert would take over as head coach of the <a href="/wiki/Ajax_Youth_Academy" title="Ajax Youth Academy">Ajax A1</a> (under-19) selection ahead of the 2016–17 season, where he would coach his son <a href="/wiki/Justin_Kluivert" title="Justin Kluivert">Justin Kluivert</a> with the team having secured placement in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Youth_League" title="UEFA Youth League">UEFA Youth League</a> the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-Voetbal_International_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Voetbal_International-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following his announcement to join Ajax, Kluivert remained head coach of Curaçao for round two of the Caribbean Cup qualifiers where they faced <a href="/wiki/Guyana_national_football_team" title="Guyana national football team">Guyana</a> and the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Virgin_Islands_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Virgin Islands national football team">U.S. Virgin Islands</a> in group 3. Curaçao won both their matches at home, defeating Guyana 5–2 and the U.S. Virgin Islands 7–0 in his final match as head coach of the island nation.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> On 14 July 2016 it was announced that Kluivert would no longer coach the under-19 team of Ajax, but that he would instead take over the position as director of football for French club <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_F.C." title="Paris Saint-Germain F.C.">Paris Saint-Germain</a>. He expressed that his intention was to stay with Ajax, but that he could not refuse the offer made by PSG.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His efforts for the national team of Curaçao did not go without merit as the team secured qualification for both the <a href="/wiki/2017_Caribbean_Cup" title="2017 Caribbean Cup">2017 Caribbean Cup</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2017_CONCACAF_Gold_Cup" title="2017 CONCACAF Gold Cup">2017 CONCACAF Gold Cup</a>, where they would compete for the first time in 40 years under the guidance of <a href="/wiki/Remko_Bicentini" title="Remko Bicentini">Remko Bicentini</a> and Kluivert.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cameroon">Cameroon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cameroon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2018 he became assistant to Clarence Seedorf at the Cameroon national team, before being sacked in July 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_Barcelona">Return to Barcelona</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Return to Barcelona">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 2019 he became the academy director of <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Kluivert has appeared in commercials for the American sportswear company <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jackson_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In 1996, he starred in a Nike commercial titled "Good vs Evil" in a gladiatorial game set in a <a href="/wiki/Roman_amphitheatre" title="Roman amphitheatre">Roman amphitheatre</a>. Appearing alongside football players from around the world, including <a href="/wiki/Ronaldo_(Brazilian_footballer)" title="Ronaldo (Brazilian footballer)">Ronaldo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Maldini" title="Paolo Maldini">Paolo Maldini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Cantona" title="Eric Cantona">Eric Cantona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Figo" title="Luís Figo">Luís Figo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Campos" title="Jorge Campos">Jorge Campos</a>, they defend "<a href="/wiki/The_Beautiful_Game" title="The Beautiful Game">the beautiful game</a>" against a team of demonic warriors, before it culminates with Cantona striking the ball and destroying evil.<sup id="cite_ref-Jackson_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Legal issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 9 September 1995, Kluivert crashed a borrowed BMW into another car in Amsterdam, killing the driver and seriously injuring a female passenger. Kluivert admitted to speeding before the crash, and was convicted of death by dangerous driving. As a consequence, he was sentenced to perform 240 hours of community service.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:174px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Kluivert_portrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2b/Patrick_Kluivert_portrait.jpg" decoding="async" width="172" height="186" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="172" data-file-height="186" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Kluivert_portrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portrait of Patrick Kluivert</div></div></div>
<p>Kluivert is the second son of former football player <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Kluivert" title="Kenneth Kluivert">Kenneth Kluivert</a>, who played for <a href="/wiki/SV_Robinhood" class="mw-redirect" title="SV Robinhood">SV Robinhood</a> in the <a href="/wiki/SVB_Topklasse" title="SVB Topklasse">SVB Hoofdklasse</a> and for the <a href="/wiki/Suriname_national_football_team" title="Suriname national football team">Suriname national team</a>. His mother Lidwina Kluivert, was born in <a href="/wiki/Willemstad" title="Willemstad">Willemstad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">Curaçao</a>, in the former <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a>, to a Surinamese father and Curaçaoan mother.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> His parents were married in <a href="/wiki/Paramaribo" title="Paramaribo">Paramaribo</a>, and both his elder siblings were born in <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, before the family emigrated to the Netherlands in 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 September 2007, Kluivert's wife Rossana Lima gave birth to a baby boy, named Shane Patrick. He has three sons, Quincy, <a href="/wiki/Justin_Kluivert" title="Justin Kluivert">Justin</a> and Ruben from his first marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Justin Kluivert played for the <a href="/wiki/Ajax_Youth_Academy" title="Ajax Youth Academy">Ajax Youth Academy</a> having won the B-juniors Eredivisie, the under-17 competition in the Netherlands, and having played in the 2015 edition of the <a href="/wiki/Copa_Amsterdam" title="Copa Amsterdam">Copa Amsterdam</a> as well. Justin has since moved on to the Italian club <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">A.S. Roma</a> since the start of the 2018-19 season.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Club">Club</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Club">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Player">Player</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Kluivert&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Player">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
